  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer9584983993564509442">Lara Cameron is a famous powerful wealthy New York building developer who struggled from brutal poverty in Glace Bay, a banker who took her body as part of her first deal, to Chicago, banker Keller whose love she takes lightly for granted.   <span id="freeText9584983993564509442" style="display:none">Lara Cameron is a famous powerful wealthy New York building developer who struggled from brutal poverty in Glace Bay, a banker who took her body as part of her first deal, to Chicago, banker Keller whose love she takes lightly for granted. As her skyscrapers and boutique hotels tower on earth, she is at the top of a male dominated field. She lies and cheats to close a deal, making cruel enemies. She is forty, beautiful, glamorous, insecure, ruthless, vulnerable, secretly generous, rich - and still wants more. She marries an international concert pianist, the Lochinvar of her childhood dreams, but someone puts him in the hospital and threatens to take down her empire.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_162031822" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162031822" />
    <a title="kwesi 章英狮" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4218875-kwesi"><img alt="kwesi 章英狮" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549853625p2/4218875.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162031822?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kwesi 章英狮" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kwesi 章英狮" href="/user/show/4218875-kwesi">kwesi 章英狮</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688084905" href="/book/show/1795294.The_Stars_Shine_Down">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4218875-kwesi?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4218875-kwesi?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4218875-kwesi?shelf=sidney-sheldon">sidney-sheldon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162031822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6514850271838814154">I promised myself not to write a review, but GR is so tempting. I'm currently sitting, waiting, waiting for the right time to stand. Imagining the high buildings, the towers and even the tallest skyscraper built in Dubai. <i>I can't pronounce the word skyscraper, boo.</i> A skyscraper is a tall, habitable building, no definite height as long as it gets higher and higher.<br/><br/>One of the most iconic and popular skyscraper built in New York was the <i>World Trade Center</i>. Built on 1973 and stood for 23 years after</span>
  <span id="freeText6514850271838814154" style="display:none">I promised myself not to write a review, but GR is so tempting. I'm currently sitting, waiting, waiting for the right time to stand. Imagining the high buildings, the towers and even the tallest skyscraper built in Dubai. <i>I can't pronounce the word skyscraper, boo.</i> A skyscraper is a tall, habitable building, no definite height as long as it gets higher and higher.<br><br>One of the most iconic and popular skyscraper built in New York was the <i>World Trade Center</i>. Built on 1973 and stood for 23 years after the great suicide attack forcing it to collide in full height causing thousands of deaths and millions of mourners to pray for the soul and the survivors. It was one of the worst terrorist attack happened, when the news flashed a picture of <i>Bin Laden</i> informing the casualties that he died when American armies entered his territory last week my cousin said that she can't forget the days that the people mourned for the 3,000 deaths including Filipinos and some foreigners.<br><br>On September 24, 2004, the tallest skyscraper was beginning to rise through the wide sky and in 2009 it was finished with great satisfaction and named as the tallest man-made skyscraper. The <i>Burj Dubai</i> designed by <i>Adrian Smith</i> and his team creating a marvelous, luxurious habitable building defeating the tallest pyramid in Asia, <i>Great Pyramid of Giza</i>. <i>I'm not interested to buy a room in that building, remember the earthquakes.</i> In 1992, Sidney Sheldon wrote his first attempt to build a skyscraper by his well-know protagonist, <b>Lara Cameron</b>, by writing an interesting yet claimable masterpiece as she journey through man's world, real estate.<br><br><b>Lara Cameron</b>, born in Nova Scotia, her mother died in childbirth with her twin and her hopeless dad took care of her, or maybe not. She was never given any attention, no money to buy new clothes, to own things, to go to school, and secluded from other children. When her father died, she realized she have to face the future, the strength that she needed must be zipped off from her so she face her greatest challenge, to dominate man's world, real estate.<br><br>As she venture through years, meeting people, enemies and friends, losing them one by one, building skyscrapers, parks, condominiums and etc. She achieved far from what she imagined, a strong willed woman who wants to be the empress of her own kingdom as she built her structures higher and higher. But when a tragedy happened to her husband, she soon been accused causing herself to carry the weights. Can she survive in the end or another destiny that the Faiths destined to her to suffer like her father?<br><br>A very interesting and commercially written for everyone to enjoyed, not only for female but to everyone who really interested in reading a fast-paced and informative book. The beginning until the end, the book was so boring keeping you to continue reading but the near end was so shockingly interesting. Sidney Sheldon cannot missed such great writing style, pulling the readers till the end and giving twisted lines. A must read!<br><br><a href="http://oldfashionedreader.blogspot.com/2011/05/stars-shine-down-by-sidney-sheldon.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348592i/702824._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3149914164" />
    <a title="Martina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3939397-martina"><img alt="Martina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325947875p2/3939397.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3149914164?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Martina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Martina" href="/user/show/3939397-martina">Martina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3939397-martina?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3149914164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16736165434334681296">Just like Sheldon's other novels, <i>The stars shine down</i> is a light read, with the pages literally flying by. But apart from its utter readability, it offers little substance and even less tension than other works by Sheldon. I know Sheldon's novels are fluffy reads we consume for fun, but I still prefer more suspense and twists. This novel is pretty much a flat line - after overcoming her unfortunate beginning, Lara Cameron barely has any obstacles. And if she does encounter a hiccup here and the</span>
  <span id="freeText16736165434334681296" style="display:none">Just like Sheldon's other novels, <i>The stars shine down</i> is a light read, with the pages literally flying by. But apart from its utter readability, it offers little substance and even less tension than other works by Sheldon. I know Sheldon's novels are fluffy reads we consume for fun, but I still prefer more suspense and twists. This novel is pretty much a flat line - after overcoming her unfortunate beginning, Lara Cameron barely has any obstacles. And if she does encounter a hiccup here and there, it's all handled efficiently, usually by telephoning the <i>deus ex machina</i>, Paul Martin. The main intrigue kicks in relatively late in the novel and by that time we all suspect what's going on.<br /><br />In terms of rating, this book would ideally be a 2.5 stars. Even though it's better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3105204981?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>A stranger in the mirror</i>
</a> in several aspects, it's still doesn't top <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109702430" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The naked face</i>
</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16736165434334681296" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer458980654" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13240183325545110823">Stunningly beautiful Lara Cameron on her fortieth birthday, having just lost her fame and fortune as foremost (only female) building developer in Chicago, then New York, her name plastered on the highest deluxe hotels and offices, reviews her life. Born unwanted to an impoverished drunk in Glace Bay, she takes over his rent collection when he is dying. Her first banker, ugly and fat, makes her first deal dependent on having her virgin body. I almost gave up reading. <br/><br/>Her Chicago banker Howard Kel</span>
  <span id="freeText13240183325545110823" style="display:none">Stunningly beautiful Lara Cameron on her fortieth birthday, having just lost her fame and fortune as foremost (only female) building developer in Chicago, then New York, her name plastered on the highest deluxe hotels and offices, reviews her life. Born unwanted to an impoverished drunk in Glace Bay, she takes over his rent collection when he is dying. Her first banker, ugly and fat, makes her first deal dependent on having her virgin body. I almost gave up reading. <br /><br />Her Chicago banker Howard Keller falls in love, but she treats him as an employee. She privately helps employees with health problems, but lies and connives to get deals done, making a bad enemy of competing developer Steve Murchison. <br /><br />Union trouble leads to a long-time lover, Mafia lawyer Paul Martin 65. Apparently Sicilian Mafia began to combat corrupt government, so Ivo Martino, ten when a powerful land owner had local police torture his father, chop off his privates, stuff them in his mouth, and kill his mother too. Years later, grown powerful himself, the boy performed the same punishment on the landlord, then fled with his family to America. Was this Paul's life? No, his grandfather's. Did author research flash dollar signs so the incident had to be included? I almost quit again.<br /><br />International famous pianist Philip Adler is the living picture of Lara's childhood imaginary Lochinvar, so despite nothing in common, she wants him for a husband. I foresee trouble with Paul, and am tired of her pate and champagne, private jets and hoity toity lifestyle. I skip to the end, then check back a bit. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />Philip hospitalized after an attack, Lara blames Paul. But testifying in court, rejected Paul protects her. Jealous Howard is the mastermind villain that tried to take her down. In the car with recovered Philip, she sees a potential site, and we realize she is still ambitious and hasn't learned anything. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I could have quit at the beginning.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13240183325545110823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_739031914" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/739031914" />
    <a title="Serene Wong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11737688-serene-wong"><img alt="Serene Wong" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473342672p2/11737688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/739031914?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Serene Wong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Serene Wong" href="/user/show/11737688-serene-wong">Serene Wong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer739031914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2879086444887804998">THIS BOOK ROCKS. I can't think of any good words to say about this book actually - it is indescribable.<br/><br/>Okay, I shall go on to explain why.<br/><br/>Lara Cameron is born with a jack-ass of a father who refuses to acknowledge her in his life, calling her a "jinx" creating all sorts of problems for her. What made matters worse is that her mother had died giving birth to her, which added to all the tension. As a result, Lara grew up without a mother's love AND a father's love, being outcast by the students in</span>
  <span id="freeText2879086444887804998" style="display:none">THIS BOOK ROCKS. I can't think of any good words to say about this book actually - it is indescribable.<br /><br />Okay, I shall go on to explain why.<br /><br />Lara Cameron is born with a jack-ass of a father who refuses to acknowledge her in his life, calling her a "jinx" creating all sorts of problems for her. What made matters worse is that her mother had died giving birth to her, which added to all the tension. As a result, Lara grew up without a mother's love AND a father's love, being outcast by the students in her school who liked to bully her upon knowing she does not have any parents. Her father works at a boarding house in which he needs to collect rents from the tenants and return to the landlord at the end of the month. The boarding house is where Lara starts to become more independent - while her father nearly died (unfortunately in a bad way) resting in a hospital, Lara was the one who went around to help collect dues owed and replaced her father's position. This impressed the landlord however, he was a bastard who intend to take advantage of Lara.<br />Fast forward, Lara became an impressive owner of hotels and she managed to make her mark in a man's dominated field - real estate. The put downs and humiliation by the men she had come across had not stopped her determination to succeed. What is inspiring about this novel is that a woman's inner strength is so strong that others can't help but stop to admire and respect her.<br /><br />I feel that Lara has many good and strong points. Firstly, though she has a stoic stone cold woman facade, beneath all that lies a gold heart. This is evident in how she treats her employees as though they are her family - a family she could never have, properly.<br /><br />I am glad she finally found her happily ever after with the pianist.<br /><br />The Stars Shine Down truly deserve an accolade.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2879086444887804998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_374908670" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/374908670" />
    <a title="Alchris M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10702720-alchris-m"><img alt="Alchris M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341484068p2/10702720.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/374908670?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alchris M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alchris M." href="/user/show/10702720-alchris-m">Alchris M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer374908670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14759922236483867330">The Stars Shine Down is the story of Lara Cameron, a self-made billionaire who had dominated the world of real estate—which, according to the book, is mostly dominated by men, as portrayed in other characters used in the story. My opinions on different aspects of the story vary as follows:<br/><br/>1.) The story of Lara being from rags to riches sounds a little impossible, more like a fairy-tale-type of story. But it's Sidney's story, so I give him that right to tell his story and develop characters any w</span>
  <span id="freeText14759922236483867330" style="display:none">The Stars Shine Down is the story of Lara Cameron, a self-made billionaire who had dominated the world of real estate—which, according to the book, is mostly dominated by men, as portrayed in other characters used in the story. My opinions on different aspects of the story vary as follows:<br /><br />1.) The story of Lara being from rags to riches sounds a little impossible, more like a fairy-tale-type of story. But it's Sidney's story, so I give him that right to tell his story and develop characters any way he wanted to.<br /><br />2.) In this story, Sidney had proven himself once again as a "Wizard of Words." As a writer myself, I admire authors who can actually write detailed sex scenes without being too vulgar. Sheldon did that with his metaphor with the act of having sex to the storm and the buildings, as well as the curtains and ripples and shadows. 100 stars for that!<br /><br />3.) Relating the title to some scenes in the story somehow—as silly as it may sound—gave me tears. This is the only book that had done that to me, Sheldon being the only author. "The stars shine down and watch us live our little lives and weep for us..."<br /><br />4.) Some twists in the story were like fallacies. But that's an element in thriller and suspense writing, innit?<br /><br />4.) The ending somehow didn't leave a lasting impression to me. Or perhaps, I've expected something similar to Sidney's "The Other Side Of Midnight." It's good though that Sidney made this one less tragic.<br /><br />I'd still give Sheldon 5 stars for this novel. He's a wizard of words. I like his prose. Fantastic author. He's the only author whose genre I despise yet can still entice me to read up to the very last page.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14759922236483867330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1261562013" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1261562013?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/4182683-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1261562013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6877554936933842250">One of the reasons why I like Shidney Sheldon's books is because he usually has strong women protagonist and this book did too. The book is about a successful real estate businesswomen Lara. The book begins with an epilogue where Lara is going to celebrate her 40th birthday in the highest building of the United States, built by her. The story portrays Lara as a firm, nononsense ambitious woman who does "anything" to get her job done. Like the usual Shidney Sheldon stories, the protagonist faces </span>
  <span id="freeText6877554936933842250" style="display:none">One of the reasons why I like Shidney Sheldon's books is because he usually has strong women protagonist and this book did too. The book is about a successful real estate businesswomen Lara. The book begins with an epilogue where Lara is going to celebrate her 40th birthday in the highest building of the United States, built by her. The story portrays Lara as a firm, nononsense ambitious woman who does "anything" to get her job done. Like the usual Shidney Sheldon stories, the protagonist faces difficult situations, connects with the Mafia, becomes ridiculously rich, makes friends and enemies too. I liked how the author portrayed the background story of prime characters and described Lara's success vividly.Compared to other books, by Sheldon, this was an average one. There were no surprising elements- the stories were kind of predictable. I liked the ending of the story. Overall, a nice, light book to read.</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Martin Chuck" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Martin Chuck" href="/user/show/81211197-martin-chuck">Martin Chuck</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688084905" href="/book/show/1795294.The_Stars_Shine_Down">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/81211197-martin-chuck?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/81211197-martin-chuck?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2639101389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2963411135597404305">Sidney Sheldon is one of the best selling fiction writers of all time, with notable works like <i>Master of the Game</i>, <i>Rage of Angels</i>, and <i>The Stars Shine Down</i>. <i>Stars</i> has been credited as one of his best and has been highlighted for his portrayal of strong women, supposedly.<br/><br/><i>Stars</i> starts with a woman named Lara Cameron riding a plane in a storm. The pilot informs Lara of their situation while simultaneously notices her loose clothing amidst the conflict. The novel quickly spirals into the life of Lar</span>
  <span id="freeText2963411135597404305" style="display:none">Sidney Sheldon is one of the best selling fiction writers of all time, with notable works like <i>Master of the Game</i>, <i>Rage of Angels</i>, and <i>The Stars Shine Down</i>. <i>Stars</i> has been credited as one of his best and has been highlighted for his portrayal of strong women, supposedly.<br /><br /><i>Stars</i> starts with a woman named Lara Cameron riding a plane in a storm. The pilot informs Lara of their situation while simultaneously notices her loose clothing amidst the conflict. The novel quickly spirals into the life of Lara Cameron and all the people who helped her with her success. <br /><br />A third into the novel and Lara seems deprived of noticeable strength. Her greatest asset is her charm and beauty when talking to men (and men only) to a point where it's Sheldon's favorite plot driver. Her character is incessantly described within the limits of her voluptuous body, loose clothing, and repetitive mannerisms as compared to important male characters. Sheldon psychoanalyzes the male characters in his novel dedicating at least a whole chapter to them (because I got to at least that part) even to a point where Lara tells the psychoanalysis herself.<br /><br />I decided not to finish the book because a third through it, I was already seeing a blueprint of Sheldon's story. Lara Cameron is a female protagonist written in the eyes of a man. The plot is so preposterous that I had to ask my friends who work in real estate and corporate if women who have s*x with men of power actually get far in their career, and people can't stop laughing or scoffing at the idea. Sheldon couldn't describe a single scene either. I couldn't picture the hotel she bought or the important places Lara described or had to go to. Lara supposedly spends most of her career travelling or constructing, but Sheldon couldn't stop talking about her breasts that I forgot what the first building Lara put up looked like.<br /><br />It seems that Sheldon's writing served as a blueprint to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/630.Dan_Brown" title="Dan Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Dan Brown</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/941441.Stephenie_Meyer" title="Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener"> Stephenie Meyer</a>. They write bestsellers, not literature. Reading his novel doesn't require a dictionary or any mind work or piece of imagination for that matter. Lara basically gets admired and laid a lot that I couldn't decipher if she was an actual a real estate mogul or a sex worker. It seems though as Sheldon blurred the lines of both characters to his satisfaction. I contemplated placing his novel in erotica but I've already insulted the thriller genre by reading him.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2963411135597404305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1142441436029250227">It has been a while since I got into serious reading - and I hate myself for that. With so many things happening around, I couldn't even take a breather to touch a book, let alone read it. With the proverbial dust seeming to settle down, at last, I wanted to begin with some light, easy reads to get myself back into the groove. Picked up the e-book versions of a couple of novels that I had read as a young boy, as they were being published in vernacular in one of the weekly magazines. Never really</span>
  <span id="freeText1142441436029250227" style="display:none">It has been a while since I got into serious reading - and I hate myself for that. With so many things happening around, I couldn't even take a breather to touch a book, let alone read it. With the proverbial dust seeming to settle down, at last, I wanted to begin with some light, easy reads to get myself back into the groove. Picked up the e-book versions of a couple of novels that I had read as a young boy, as they were being published in vernacular in one of the weekly magazines. Never really knew then that I was reading the works of one of the most read, much appreciated crime writers of my time.<br /><br />The Stars Shine Down is a smooth sailing novel, sort of what they call a chick-flick, with all the ingredients that make the Hollywood click - intrigue, sex, twists and an unreal plot. Read it when you feel that you want to read just to kill time, all the while keeping your brain interested in something. An OK-for-once read!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3473449397507284584">The Iron Butterfly would do everything - everything, including the use of her body - in order to get that prime location for her business deals. The Iron Butterfly if Lara Cameron, a modern day ruthless Cinderella who thinks and works like Trump and don't give a hick to what others would think, as long as she gets what she wants.<br/><br/>From rags to riches, from Nova Scotia to Chicago to New York, Lara Cameron is an enigma. She has been one of Sidney Sheldon's anti-hero protagonist heroine that you woul</span>
  <span id="freeText3473449397507284584" style="display:none">The Iron Butterfly would do everything - everything, including the use of her body - in order to get that prime location for her business deals. The Iron Butterfly if Lara Cameron, a modern day ruthless Cinderella who thinks and works like Trump and don't give a hick to what others would think, as long as she gets what she wants.<br /><br />From rags to riches, from Nova Scotia to Chicago to New York, Lara Cameron is an enigma. She has been one of Sidney Sheldon's anti-hero protagonist heroine that you would love to meet and break. This book, The Stars Shine Down, has been one of the few Sheldon books I've owned and would occasionally read for deep thought reading. While many would think that Lara Cameron is monstrous, I thought she was a force to reckon with. Location, location, location - that's what it all matters to her. And when she meets the pianist that match her audacity, I knew that I would never forget a woman like Cameron.<br /><br />Worth reading over and over again!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3536308608" />
    <a title="Eddie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/99471885-eddie"><img alt="Eddie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599260054p2/99471885.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eddie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eddie" href="/user/show/99471885-eddie">Eddie</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15494399186486263619">Breathtaking and sensual.<br/>Sometimes you can't trust the people closest to you, when it involves the hearts and emotions.<br/>Lara Cameron aimed to be successful, to build her own empire, to owe many buildings, to go against The Fate.<br/>She proved to the world, it wasn't a fairytale when she migrated from rags to riches.<br/>She worked very closely with Howard Keller for all her projects, but she failed to acknowledge his feelings and designs on her.<br/>She got sexually involved with Paul Martin, being pampered an</span>
  <span id="freeText15494399186486263619" style="display:none">Breathtaking and sensual.<br />Sometimes you can't trust the people closest to you, when it involves the hearts and emotions.<br />Lara Cameron aimed to be successful, to build her own empire, to owe many buildings, to go against The Fate.<br />She proved to the world, it wasn't a fairytale when she migrated from rags to riches.<br />She worked very closely with Howard Keller for all her projects, but she failed to acknowledge his feelings and designs on her.<br />She got sexually involved with Paul Martin, being pampered and loved by him, but he was already married. She knew she couldn't give all her love to Paul Martin, and she knew something was missing in her life. She wanted true love, and someone she could come home to everyday. She had visualised and dreamt of one mystery man as a husband.<br />Till she met the famous pianist, Phillip Adler. It was a hurried and short-noticed marriage ceremony between them. She knew it was him who had appeared in her visual.<br />But things began to sour and life took a twist, when she started to complain of not being able to have Phillip Adler all to herself everyday and at some parties, when he had to be away on concert tours most times. That was when she started to lose her buildings, her empire started to face financial troubles, and her husband was robbed and crippled on his left hand.<br />Revenge and jealousy seems to be un separated. Who were behind her downfall???</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13317452345735240812">Dakle ovo je definitivno bila loša knjiga za mene. Dobila sam je, tako da nisu bačene pare, ali prosto meni nije legla. Ne upoznajem se sa Šeldonom prvi put, Pesak vremena mi se jako dopao, ali ova knjiga prosto nema to nešto. Prvi problem je u glavnoj junakinji koja je za mene poremećeni primer uspeha, sve što je postigla i ja se na kraju vraćam odakle je ona zapravo krenula i to mi se ne dopada. Onda i samo kretanje priče, veći deo je o njenim poslovnim planovima u kojima se zapravno ništa ne </span>
  <span id="freeText13317452345735240812" style="display:none">Dakle ovo je definitivno bila loša knjiga za mene. Dobila sam je, tako da nisu bačene pare, ali prosto meni nije legla. Ne upoznajem se sa Šeldonom prvi put, Pesak vremena mi se jako dopao, ali ova knjiga prosto nema to nešto. Prvi problem je u glavnoj junakinji koja je za mene poremećeni primer uspeha, sve što je postigla i ja se na kraju vraćam odakle je ona zapravo krenula i to mi se ne dopada. Onda i samo kretanje priče, veći deo je o njenim poslovnim planovima u kojima se zapravno ništa ne dešava, ne upoznajem nju. Ko voli lagano štivo bez da zamara mozak ok je, za mene lično ipak ne.<br /><br />So this was bad book for me, i'm sure in that. I get as gift so i can't tell that it was waste of money but still. Thi is not firs Sidney Sheldon book took, i already read The Sands of Time and i did like that one, but this one just does not have that X factor for me. First (and main) problem is in main the heroine, who for me is just not good example for success, even with all good she done i still could not help myslef but return on how she get all that. Then just the way story goes i read on 100 pages about building process when i want to see her soul and who she is. Who loves that type of books will do just fine, but for me no it's just not my cup of tea :)</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('O6qN2P861aqCuRdUhPhQndISjmjXqFHIHjbVnFovmhUhKq9xIdYehYP2h9qPR8eGxtffk3JC6gpH/Wcv1Ki04g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('n9TZYahCnUvBQgWcGZrpKVoZeXJGDHa1+2xEKKUomw2FVPvIdq5WZMANlRISJX4yTtwoiePmzXeip/abK6+1+g==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer12311583955120649546">Sidney Sheldon (1917-2007) was an American writer who won awards in three careers—a Broadway playwright, a Hollywood TV and movie screenwriter, and a best-selling novelist.<br/><br/>His TV works spanned a twenty-year period during which he created <i>I Dream of Jeannie</i> (1965-70), <i>Hart to Hart</i> (1979-84), and <i>The Patty Duke Show</i> (1963-66), but it was not until after he turned 50 and began writing best-selling no</span>
  <span id="freeText12311583955120649546" style="display:none">Sidney Sheldon (1917-2007) was an American writer who won awards in three careers—a Broadway playwright, a Hollywood TV and movie screenwriter, and a best-selling novelist.<br /><br />His TV works spanned a twenty-year period during which he created <i>I Dream of Jeannie</i> (1965-70), <i>Hart to Hart</i> (1979-84), and <i>The Patty Duke Show</i> (1963-66), but it was not until after he turned 50 and began writing best-selling novels such as <i>Master of the Game</i> (1982), <i>The Other Side of Midnight</i> (1973) and <i>Rage of Angels</i> (1980) that he became most famous.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12311583955120649546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
